field--string-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">This lesson plan is designed to use the story of Genesis to instill an understanding that faith does not undermine science and science does not undermine faith. By using images of nature, students will gain an appreciation for the spark of wonder and awe that can come from marveling at God’s creation. Students will then apply their newfound understanding to a creative project that includes a reflection which describes their experience of wonder and awe regarding creation.</div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li> <p>Develop an appreciation for God’s continuous creation  </p> </li> <li> <p>Gain an awareness that the Bible is a collection of books written by various authors at different times for unique audiences and should be read as such </p> </li> <li> <p>Understand that each portion of the Bible is part of a whole story, should be read with regard to its context, and has one collective aim, which is our salvation </p> </li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li> <p>Analyze images to develop a model which expresses wonder at God’s creation  </p> </li> <li> <p>Articulate the Catholic concept that describes the intersection of faith and reason using our creation story as an example</p> </li> <li> <p>Compare and contrast the creation accounts to show the relational unity of faith and reason and how that is essential to our Catholic faith </p> </li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p>Introduction / Video / Discussion: </p> <ul> <li> <p>Introduction of lesson with power point (see attached file)</p> </li> <li> <p>Viewing of video (“Awe and Wonder”) - linked in power point </p> </li> <li> <p>Discussion (see notes section in attached power point) </p> </li> </ul> <p>Image Cards:</p> <ul> <li> <p>Teacher has students choose an image from nature which expresses something about how they see themselves  </p> </li> <li> <p>In pairs each student will show her image to her partner and explain why she chose it; then her partner will ask further/deeper questions regarding her choice of image; then students switch roles </p> </li> <li> <p>Teacher gives prompt for students to write a brief reflection on how the image they chose for themselves connects to the theme of wonder at God’s creation </p> </li> </ul> <p>Newspaper Example:</p> <ul> <li> <p>Teacher brings in physical newspaper and flips through the different section and asks students what the purpose of that section is and how they would read it (Example: front page/comic section/obits/op-ed/ad for tires; Ask students: Would we read this as news? Why is this in the paper at all/what's it's purpose?)</p> </li> </ul> <p>Genesis 1 and 2:</p> <ul> <li> <p>Read Genesis 1 and 2 together in class (or assign for homework if class time does not allow)  </p> </li> <li> <p>Discussion: How are the two chapters different? This raises a lot of questions today about evolution. Why do people not believe in evolution? What are their concerns? Talk about how we are integrated in the rest of creation. Here’s what the church says / here’s how the church interprets the story of genesis / what’s the purpose of these texts.</p> </li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li>Students will create an art project that illustrates in some way what they’ve learned about creation. In addition, students will write a 1 page reflection on their experience of seeing creation from the perspective of wonder. </li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Standards</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li>Refer to USCCB curriculum for 9-12 for standards </li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Essential Questions</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li> <p>How can images of God’s creation inspire awe and wonder? </p> </li> <li> <p>What does nature tell us about our relationship with God and all creation? </p> </li> <li> <p>How do the creation accounts show the relational unity of faith and reason and how that is field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">The purpose of the Lesson Plan is to have students explore the concepts of Creation through Genesis 1. Students will develop an understanding that through prior knowledge of Darwin’s Theory of Evolution that Faith and Science do not contradict one another. In actuality both concepts work together to compliment and give a full understanding of God’s complete participation in Creation by identifying primary and secondary causality. Students will be able to articulate why Genesis 1 and Darwin’s theory of evolution are not contradictory. <br /> </div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students can articulate the essential truths/doctrines of the Catholic faith that can be derived from the story of Genesis. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Demonstrate a basic awareness of Darwin’s Theory of Evolution by natural selection.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Understand that different disciplines of knowledge are able to answer different types of questions.  </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Identify the concepts of primary and secondary causes. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Recognize the defining characteristics of a human soul. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long evolution. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Demonstrate complementarity of evolution and creation </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Discuss “What is the Human Being?” </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Describe how evolution doesn’t negate the possibility of a divinely created cosmos using the ideas of primary and secondary causes . </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Synthesize their knowledge of natural selection to what they read in Genesis. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Distinguish between biological and theological humans. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Describe how evolution is an ordered process and that chance can be a sign of DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Lesson Plan Method</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Bell Work (5 minutes) </span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The following discussion question will be posted on the students online learning management platform. They should respond to it quickly with a “first impressions” mentality. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><em><span>Based on your own prior knowledge, express your first impression or current understanding of evolution and the story of creation in Genesis. Do you believe that the theory of evolution is compatible with what is read in Genesis? Why or why not? </span></em></span></span></span></span></p> <ol start="2"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lecture on Genesis 1 with Google Slides presentation (40 minutes)</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will take Cornell style notes  </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Resource 1: Google Slides Presentation - contains content of the lecture. Additional content and examples are included in the speaker notes section of the presentation. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Exit ticket/formative assessment (10 minutes) </span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Respond to the bell work question on a second post with updated knowledge or evidence learned from today’s class. This post should be more thoughtful and include a thoughtful argument/explanation. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>HW/Assessment - Students will come prepared for a socratic seminar on 2 paragraph’s from Benedict XVI’s 3rd homily from “In the Beginning” the following day. </span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>During the seminar, each student will be assigned one student to watch/follow and will be responsible for evaluating their participation using the rubric provided. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Resource 2: Reading material to prepare for the seminar </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Resource 3: Rubric for socratic seminar </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> </ol> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>All three resources are attached below in the resource section </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span><span><span>The formal assessment will consist of a socratic method the day following the lesson. The students will discuss the reading assignment of two paragraphs from the third homily of Ratzinger's,</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>  In the Beginning</span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> and Genesis 1. Resource 2 contains the content of the reading for the seminar. Resource 3 contains a peer and self evaluation rubric. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">This is a lesson that introduces the Creation account of Genesis and the Theory of Evolution showing that the two are compatible. There are short readings for homework, class discussions based on the reading, small group discussion, a short Natural Selection activity, and a final discussion leading students to the conclusion that the two are compatible. </div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lesson 1: 90 mins</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li>Prior to Lesson, assign as homework: "Survival of the Sickest" Chapter 1, found in Files.</li> </ol> <p>Day of the Lesson</p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Pre Assessment (10 mins)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Warm up: Students write a response to these questions and be prepared to discuss them.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Explain, in your own words, the Theory of Evolution by natural selection as proposed by Charles Darwin?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>List at least 3 things you know about human evolution.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What do the Creation accounts in Genesis state?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>If something is true, what does that mean?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Small Group Discussion (10 mins)</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Review the Pre assessment as a group</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>On the board, write down commonalities discovered in the small group discussion</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Go around the room to discuss the common themes uncovered</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>3. Based on responses, teacher goes over misconceptions and areas of sustainment</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Look for the following misconceptions:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The Theory of Evolution is only a theory and a weak explanation</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Humans evolved from monkeys, chimps, or modern primates</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The Creation accounts are literal stories of the beginning of the universe</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Creation Story Emphasis</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>4. USCCB Understanding the Bible</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Genres in the Bible</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What is a myth?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Explain Genesis as symbolic cosmogony</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Write your own Cosmogony</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Understand uniqueness of Creation accounts</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Theory of Evolution Emphasis</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>5. “Survival of the Sickest” book discussion</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Formative assessment over Ch 1 of book found in Files</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What specifically demonstrates natural selection in the story of hemochromatosis? How is this a model of how a population evolves?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Why did hemochromatosis become more common throughout Europe during the Middle Ages?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Explain how a trait can increase survival and reproduction (fitness)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What could be other examples of natural selection that you know from your own experience?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Phet Activity - Use the Natural Selection Lab found in Files.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Post Activity Discussion:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>6. Write a dialogue:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Write a dialogue about the apparent conflict between the Genesis creation account and the scientific theory of human evolution.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Use three characters:</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Danny – A high school student who believes that Darwin’s theory of evolution by natural selection has made the Genesis account into nonsense</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Steve – A high school student who believes that Scripture is must be read literally, and that the plain meaning of Scripture must be believed even if it means denying the clear consensus of science</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Tim – A high school student who explains how reading Genesis as symbolic cosmogony and understanding evolution correctly can lead to a deeper understanding of science and appreciation of faith</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> </ol> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>By the end, students must understand the following:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Literal vs metaphorical </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Natural selection is the main driving force of Evolution.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Living thing will follow the rules of Natural Selection.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Science does not tell us why the rules exist so we must find it philosophically and theologically.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">This lesson seeks to display the complementarity of science and religion. Students will learn to appreciate God as the author of both Creation, and as an aspect of creation, science-- in particular evolution. Using a variety of resources and approaches, students will be asked to reevaluate their thoughts about faith and science in light of what the Church teaches about evolution.</div> </div> <!-- END <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Scripture</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>: (3 Minutes) GN 1:24-31</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will read using “popcorn reading” as a class.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol start="2"> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Prayer</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>: (2 Minutes)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span> St. Thomas Aquinas Prayer for before Study</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Creator of all things,</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>true Source of light and wisdom,</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>lofty origin of all being,</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>graciously let a ray of Your brilliance</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>penetrate into the darkness of my understanding</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>and take from me the double darkness</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>in which I have been born,</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>an obscurity of both sin and ignorance.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Give me a sharp sense of understanding,</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>a retentive memory,</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>and the ability to grasp things correctly and fundamentally.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Grant me the talent of being exact in my explanations,</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>and the ability to express myself with thoroughness and charm.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Point out the beginning,</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>direct the progress,</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>and help in completion;</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>through Christ our Lord.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Amen.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <ol start="3"> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Exploration of Question 1: (20 minutes)</span></span></strong></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Hook Question presented using Google Slides, present the First slide with question: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Are Creation and Evolution compatible?</span></em></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Ask students to participate in “Think, Pair, Share” (2 Minutes)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Show this video: (8 Minutes) </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://youtu.be/L_b9tWrFpj4"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Are Creation and Evolution Compatible? w/ Fr. Thomas Davenport, O.P. (Aquinas 101)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Conversation and Analysis: (10 Minutes)</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students determine from Darwin’s excerpt whether he thought evolution required a God or not.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Reflection:</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Exploration of Question 2: Return to scripture with new eyes after discussion of </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><em><span>Are Creation and Evolution Compatible?</span></em></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span> (20 minutes)</span></span></strong></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><em><span>Question: What Truths are presented in the first chapters of Genesis that explain how we are to understand the communion between God as Creator and Man as His creation?</span></em></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Read Genesis </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>GN 1:24-31 &amp; GN 2:7-8, 15-25</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lecture what it means to be made in the “image and likeness” of God. </span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>We are directly related to God, Our Father, who loves us as a father loves his children.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>We are like God in that we have a rational soul and the capacity to know and love God.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Human life possesses great sacredness due to God’s breath animating the body with a soul.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Man is made for communion with God which is meant to be his permanent state.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lecture what God’s two divine commands to Man.</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>As rational creatures, we can respond to God with “Amen!” or “So be it!” (Baglow, 58). </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>“be fertile and multiply; fill the earth”</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>“subdue it” of God’s creation; dominion and stewardship</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Man is the pinnacle of Creation which is one of the reasons why he is unique.</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>“The mystery reveals a truth that science could never discover but that faith and reason together can discern: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Homo sapiens</span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> is the ulitmate reason for why the univers exitst, the point of God’s creative activity” (Baglow, 74). </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> </ol> </li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Exploration of Question 3: Lecture on Church Teaching (20 Minutes)</span></span></strong></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Question</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>What does the Church say about creation narrative, which helps us understand what science has proposed and demonstrated in evolution? </span></em></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>To answer this question, we are turning to </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Humane Generis</span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>, a Papal encyclical of Pius XII (1950)</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What is Humani Generis: Humani generis is a papal encyclical that is "concerning some false opinions threatening to undermine the foundations of Catholic Doctrine". This document is concerned with the rising Nouvelle Théologie which will go on to have great influence at the Second Vatican Council starting during the following decade. The document itself deals directly with evolution and outlines permissible points for promulgation (</span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humani_generis"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>wikipedia</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>). </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Summary Statements: Break students into groups to read and summarize §36 and §37, as well as the warning found in §38.</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>§36: We may speculate on the origins of man’s human body as coming from “pre-existent and living matter” but must firmly hold that man’s soul comes directly from God.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>§37: We must hold that the human race as it stands today, are the descendants of first parents whom God had raised to a higher life through the inbreathing of the spiritual soul. These first parents freely rejected God’s commands to committ original sin. As their descendents, we inherit original sin.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>§38: Warns of a liberal reading of Genesis as anything other than a history that conveys Truths about God and Man. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The document then clearly states that “the Teaching Authority of the Church does not forbid that, in conformity with the present state of human sciences and sacred theology, research and discussions, on the part of men experienced in both fields, take place with regard to the doctrine of evolution” so long as we hold the Truths outlined above (HG, 36). </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Assessment</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>: Google Classroom Video w/Questions (20 (Aquinas 101)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>What are the 4 kinds of objections to faith in God shared by Prof. Karin creation?</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Summary and Analysis: (12 Minutes)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> </ol> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will read and reflect the following article by Berta M. Moritz on St. John Henry Newman </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://www.catholicscientists.org/idea/saint-john-henry-newman-a-co-patron-for-scientists"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Saint John Henry Newman: A Co-patron for Scientists?</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></li> </ol> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>“Truth cannot be contrary to truth.”</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>“I believe in design because I believe in God; not in a God because I see design.”</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>“Evolution is not inconsistent with divine design - It is accidental to us, not to God.”</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <ol start="7"> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Conclusion: Final Thoughts</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span> (5 minutes) </span></span></strong></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Pope Emeritus Benedict XVI (Homily at the Mass for the Inauguration of the Pontificate, 24 April 2005)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>“[O]nly where God is seen does life truly begin. Only when we meet the living God in Christ do we know what life is. We are not some casual and meaningless product of evolution. Each of us is the result of a thought of God. Each of us is willed, each of us is loved, each of us is necessary.”</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Briefly describe how the Biblical account of Creation and Evolution are complementary. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <p> </p> <ol start="2"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>How does being made in God’s image and likeness allow for communion between God and Man? Explain. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <p> </p> <ol start="3"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Based on </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Humani Generis,</span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> what position must we hold about man’s creation?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <p> </p> <ol start="4"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Pope Benedict XVI insists that you are not merely a product of random science. Created in the image and likeness of God (CCC, nos. 356-359, 1700-1706). 1) God made them male and female (CCC, nos. 369-373, 1605, 1702, 2331). 2) Dignity of both men and women: similarities and differences (CCC, nos. 2333-2336). 3) Contributions to the world and to the Church (CCC, nos. 2346-2347).</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Human beings as the summit of creation. b. Human persons are a body-soul unity; this reflects the physical and spiritual realities in the world (CCC, nos. 356-368).</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Evolution/Science Standards:</span></span></strong></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The Church teaches us how to relate truths of faith to science.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>There can be no conflict between religious truth and scientific and historical truth (CCC, no. 159).</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The difference between the Catholic understanding of Scripture and that of those who interpret the Bible in an overly literalist, fundamentalist way or with an approach limited to a symbolic understanding.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span> Revelation as found in the book of Genesis. B. Genesis 1–11 conveys religious truth rather than science (CCC, nos. 283-289).</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Revelation as found in the book of Genesis. C. The book reveals truth about which science and history can only speculate.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <drupal-render-placeholder callback="flag.link_builder:build" arguments="0=node&amp;1=272&amp;2=favorite_lessons" token="xV0HzGDr30rXeAcydGH6JUXE70VQpsNkRuuTPBO6d8g"></drupal-render-placeholder> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-resources--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-resources.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-resources.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-resources field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Lesson Resources</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Bible--Ignatius Press Revised Standard Version, 2nd Catholic Edition </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><em><span>Humani Generis</span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>-- Pp. class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span><span>Day 1 - </span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span>Engage/Bell Ringer - What is human evolution?  Written on board</span></span></span></span></span>. <span><span><span><span><span>Students will discuss in small groups (3-4) this question, then share with the class in a discussion - discuss whether students are giving a biological or theological explanation of evolution. </span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span>Introduce Essential Questions.</span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span>Powerpoint presentation on biological evolution - main mechanism of natural selection, mutations - will provide a link to powerpoint</span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span>Video on rock pocket mice from Biointeractive: </span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://www.biointeractive.org/classroom-resources/making-fittest-natural-selection-and-adaptation">The Making of the Fittest: Natural Selection and Adaptation</a></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span>practice worksheet on natural selection and mutations - </span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://ndfaithscience.com/sites/default/files/2021-07/IDGquiz_NaturalSelection.pdf">IDGquiz_NaturalSelection.pdf</a><span><span><span><span><span> - plan to turn in at end of class</span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span>HW: watch </span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://youtu.be/GonMs1fjMrI"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>The Purposeful Universe - A Conversation with Dr. Dan Kuebler</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a> and answer the questions below(will be on Canvas): <ul> <li> <p><span><span><span><span><span>How is evolution not <strong>truly </strong>random?</span></span></span></span></span></p> </li> <li> <p>What does convergence mean in regard to evolution?</p> </li> <li> <p>How could theology help you gain an understanding of evolution in a <strong>different </strong>way?</p> </li> </ul> </li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Day 2 - </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Engage/Bell ringer - </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Discussion on the video questions; Taking good responses and less good responses and discuss with the class a few of the responses to the Canvas.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lecture→ explain philosophical notion of primary and secondary causality (vertical and horizontal) with example of Romeo and Juliet.</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Why does Romeo commit suicide? Is the cause Romeo or is it Shakespeare?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Worksheet (attached)---students will identify 2 examples of primary and secondary causality.</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>One example will be from a novel they have read</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>One will be from a TV show/film</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Is there a way in which this distinction also applies to the Sacramental life of Christians? Think of a sacramental example.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>HW: Read p. 193-195 in <em>Faith, Science, and Reason: Theology on the Cutting Edge</em> by Chris Baglow; answer a few questions online on Canvas. Canvas questions are as follows:</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Explain the distinction the author makes between "evolution" and "evolutionism</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Although Catholics are at liberty to accept evolution, what is the only thing Catholics must believe about the evolution of the human race?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What crucial insight did John Paul II offer in terms of understanding the evolution of the human person?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Pope Benedict XVI, while accepting the scientific evidence in favor of evolution, points out that evolution does not answer which sorts of questions?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> </ol> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Day 3-</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Review the basic doctrine of the Church on the soul as it pertains to evolution</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The human body is created by God through mediate causes (human parents)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The soul is immediately created by God</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>In human beings, we see an "ontological leap". Human beings represent not just a difference in degree on the evolutionary chart, but a difference in kind.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Science, as a discipline, is unable to answer the "why" of the existence of natural things, or to identify meaning/purpose within things of the natural order.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Using a graphic organizer or illustration, students will summarize what they have learned over the last 2 days to be turned in.</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Randomly choose 3 students to present their graphic organizer</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> </li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">We are creating three 50-minute lessons (with 2 science lessons beforehand for prior knowledge) that will fit at the end of the 9th grade year in Biology and correlate with the 9th grade Introduction to the Bible class. In this cross-curricular lesson, the Bible class will revisit the Genesis account now having been through a survey of the Hebrew and Christian Scriptures. Developmentally, we hope the end of the year 9s will be more ready to see connections across departments and that they will not be as influenced by a rote or literal reading of the Creation account. These lessons will serve as an introduction to the topic of evolution from both the religious and scientific perspective, and may lead further to a cross-departmental elective on the topic.</div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>To discern and articulate theological concepts present in the Genesis creation narratives (role of God, concept of personhood, nature of creation, etc.).</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>To articulate the concepts of Evolution and Theistic Evolution and to compare and contrast them with Creationism.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>To become familiar with the general teachings of the Catholic Church on the compatibility of faith and reason, or religion and science, and to be able to articulate such.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>To recognize the future possibilities in science and technology, perhaps in the field of AI and genetic engineering, and to infer moral/ethics limits on human activity in those areas in light of the dignity of the human person.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>To become familiar with the standard and commonly accepted evidence and history of the theory of evolution. </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>To develop and use different methods of biblical exegesis or reading and interpreting the Genesis narratives (historical criticism, literary criticism, philological criticism, etc.)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>To apply messages of religious truth to modern concepts in science and technology. </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>To analyze Church documents, such as papal writings on faith and reason, and to draw conclusions regarding the compatibility of science and religion.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>To recognize and demonstrate an awareness of the limitations and dangers of a fundamentalist approach to Scripture.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>To apply the scientific evidence of evolution to the creation myth in a way that sees the two as compatible and two ways of seeing truth.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Class #1: </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Science Pre-Lesson - A Scientific Introduction to the Theory of Evolution</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Prior Knowledge: (2 class periods)</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>This lesson is designed to take place at the start of the 9th grade Biology Evolution Unit.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The purpose of this first lesson is to introduce students to the scientific theory of evolution and to the scientists that contributed to its discovery, as well as begin to understand how evolution occurs.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Reading/Assignment Due:</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>HW Due: </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://www.sciencenewsforstudents.org/article/superbugs-silent-health-emergency"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Superbugs: A Silent Health Emergency</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Questions to Answer:</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Antibiotics are supposed to be good. What is causing antibiotics to not be so “good” anymore? Give an example from the article. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Define antibiotic resistance. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The author mentioned the terms “evolution” and “survival of the fittest”: explain in your own words how you think these two terms are related to antibiotic resistance. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> </ul> </li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Body of Presentation: </span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Class discussion (15 mins): Discuss article answers. Transition to term “evolution”: what does it mean when something “evolves”? (Answer: change over time)</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What are some examples of things that “change over time”? (Ex. technology, fashion)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>How has bacteria evolved, according to the article? </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Think/Pair/Share (10 mins): What do you know about the evolution of life? Has life changed in the past 100 years? 1000 years? 1 million years? </span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Write shared answers on board via concept map</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Video</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>:</span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XOiUZ3ycZwU"><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>“The Origin of Species: The Making of a Theory”</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will be taking notes on the two scientists they will be observing: Charles Darwin &amp; Alfred Wallace</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Mini Lecture: History of the “discovery” of the Theory of Evolution, Natural Selection and Descent with Modification</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>HW: Finish Notes (Recorded Video)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Class #2: Scientific Evolution Follow-up</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Do Now: </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>The Theory of Evolution can be a challenging idea for religious people to understand. As a student in a Catholic school, what could the religious see as “conflicting” in the scientific theory? </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>T/P/S</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Video:</span></span></strong></span></span></span><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZLoZc5DIU9o"><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>The Draper-White Conflict Thesis</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will make lists in 3 columns: Things they agree with/understand, Things they disagree with/find challenging, and things they have questions about</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Fishbowl Activity</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>HW: Reflection Questions</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Class #3: Religion Lesson - On the Compatibility of Religion &amp; Science (Faith and Reason)</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Reading/Assignment Due:</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Worksheet on the Catholic Church and Faith and Reason</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Do Now: </span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>True/False Quick Questions</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>1) The Catholic Church agrees that evolution is an acceptable theory.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>2) It is only in the last decade since Pope Francis has declared that the Church accepts the connections between faith and science, such as evolution.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Discuss Homework on the Church on Faith and Reason</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Body of Presentation: See PowerPoint Slides:</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Review the passages from Church documents, take questions</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Review the history of the debate on evolution and the historically imposed conflict between science and religion. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Discuss the three ways of responding to the supposed conflict between science and religion: Against, Toward, and Away</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Ensure students grasp the difference between Creationism, Intelligent Design, and Theistic Evolution.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Quiz &amp; Activity:</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Q: If you had a roommate in college who believed in Creationism, what would that mean they believe about the Bible and the science of creation? How might you react to this information? If they asked you what you believe about creation, what would you say?</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Be prepared to share a line or two of your thinking with the class or to ask a question of your classmates.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from questions on a worksheet to gather what the students think prior to learning.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>2-questions True/False quick quiz field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Essential Questions</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>How can evolutionary theory be compatible with the hermeneutic tradition in its symbolic and theological interpretation of Genesis 1-3 in the Catholic tradition? </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>How can the goodness of God and God’s creation be maintained (a central tenet of Genesis 1) in light of the theory of evolution by natural selection? Can evolutionary theory contribute to the Catholic notion of a divinely created universe?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>How should humans be considered the pinnacle of God’s creation? How does evolution change the way we should think about this Scriptural teaching (i.e. humans being created in the image of God)?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What are the ramifications of the Genesis Creation account on how we view the human person in light of our technological age? How can we maintain our sense of duty and purpose to creation in this ever-changing world? </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">The purpose of this lesson is to begin a dialogue with students about the conflict between Faith and Science before entering a study of biological evolution. After a brief introductory lecture about the Church’s relationship with science, including consideration of primary and secondary causality, students will engage with primary Church sources and articulate the Church’s position on biological evolution. This is designed for a 90 minute block period but could easily be adapted for a 45-50 minute class. (Nolan Catholic High School)</div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">This lesson will be covered in 2- 80 minute Freshmen Theology class and 2-80 minute Freshmen Biology classes, with separate assessment portions. This lesson explores the relationship of the doctrine of creation and the Earth’s history of events. In theology, freshmen students will explore Genesis Chapter 1. The goal of the lesson will be to look at the time in the Bible and the progression from disorder and chaos to order and harmony and the “days” of creation will impact the other events of the other days in creation. Biology will examine the geologic time scale in order to observe the slow and varied pace of events as well as their relatedness. Through engagement in the lessons from both subject areas, the student will be taking a look as the connections rather than the contradictions of creation and evolution.<br /> <br /> <br /> </div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>1. Compare and contrast evolution in the Biblical sense vs. evidence in science</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>2. Demonstrate an understanding of the “The Gap” Theory</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>3. Describe the role of evolution in your life as a Christian </span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>4. Articulate the Catholic concept of Creation</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>1.Evaluate evidence of evolution related to the Christian story</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>2. Synthesize the coexistence of evolution and creation in the 21st Century</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>3. To create a model of time in the Creation story vs. geologic time scale</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>4. Analyze the connection of the scientific conservatism laws to the existence of a Creator.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lesson Timing:  2- 80 minute classes in the freshman theology class/ 2- 80 minute classes with discussions/activities for the freshman Biology class portion</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>PURPOSE: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>To make connections between the story of creation and the organization of how the Earth evolved and organisms formed</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lesson Plan structure: Day 1 for Theology class</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>HOOK- Use of St. John’s Bible Creation illumination of Creation to ask students “What do you notice? What do you wonder? What do you observe?” What would you title the image of this piece of art?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span> Class Activity: Read Genesis chapter 1 and review “In the Beginning” Gospel on creation</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Small group: create a visual of chapter 1  on chart poster paper(illustrate or write out what their interpretation looks like)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Day 2:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Finish timelines if needed</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Gallery walk to view peer timelines and provide positive criticism for reflection/comparison of ideas</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Reflect on their feedback to their timelines</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Class discussion: “ What is your interpretation of how creation occurred?”</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Assessment: Exit ticket- personal reflection of what the class discussion means to that individual student</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Freshman Biology class</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Day 3 and 4: HOOK-”How old is the Earth? How do you know?”</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will be given a table of events of Earth’s major fossil contributions based on the different eras, periods, and epochs to be able to draw the fossil record to scale using a long roll of toilet paper and having them count out each “square” is equal to “X” number of million years passing. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will draw an illustrated image to represent the major fossils within the fossil record once the timeline has been numbered.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Bring back out the theology class images of creation to compare to the timeline of Earth</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Class discussion: How does the timeline of Earth’s time relate to our story of Creation images from previous class?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><br /> <br /> <br />  </p> <p> </p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * theology classes: Students will be creating a personal reflection of their interpretation of rationality of the organization of Creation in the book of Genesis and incorporate the artist’s view of the St. John’s Bible illumination of Creation by incorporating the essential questions.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>In the Biology class: Students will be creating a CER  focusing on the essential questions to make observations and conclusions comparing the timeline of Earth’s history to their thoughts about Genesis Creation passage.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p> </p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Essential Questions</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>1. How does the Catholic Church’s teaching on  creation relate to but also differ from the scientific theory of evolution?</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>2. How does an understanding of primary and secondary causality help to relate the various “laws of nature” (of physics, chemistry, biology, etc.) to God’s transcendent, creative action?</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>3. Why should the Church be concerned with synthesizing natural, scientific knowledge with the revealed truths of faith in Scripture and Tradition?</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p>
