<!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--field-lesson-time--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-description--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-description.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-description.html.twig * field--string-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">This lesson explores the scientific understanding of the evolution of the cosmos and the whole of history as the timeless act of God’s Divine Creation. As well as, the understanding that the universe is created both by and for Christ. During this activity, students will be spaced out along a football field (or equivalent area) in spaces representing events in cosmological time, geological time, evolutionary time, human history, and salvation history. </div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><strong><span><span><span>Theological Knowledge: </span></span></span></strong></p> <p><span><span><span>1.  Articulate the proper understanding of the Catholic doctrine of creation.</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>2. Recognize the ways in which revelation occurs in various moments in evolutionary and human history. </span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>3. Understand the difference between Natural and Divine Revelation.</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>4. Understand and articulate that all of creation (including cosmological history) is “Christ-centered,” i.e. that Christ/salvation is the ultimate end (purpose/goal) of the entirety of creation.</span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><strong><span><span><span>Scientific Knowledge:</span></span></span></strong></p> <p><span><span><span>1. Visualizing the age of the earth including major events in the evolution of living things.</span></span></span></p> <p><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN"><span><span>2. Creating visual representations to scale which allow for better comprehension and evaluation of concept.</span></span></span></p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN"><span><span>1. Compare and contrast the difference between natural revelation and Divine Revelation.<br /> <br /> 2. Determine the role of the human being in light of natural revelation and Divine Revelation.<br /> <br /> 3. Build a model of the evolutionary history of the cosmos, the Earth,  human evolution and salvation history.<br /> <br /> 4. Understand the Prologue of the Gospel of John, the Divine <em>Logos</em>, and the Catholic Doctrine of Creation from a new perspective. </span></span></span></p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN"><span>Background:</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>This lesson is designed for a senior-level elective course, specifically a Faith/Science elective—though this activity could be used in any senior Theology elective or upper-division science course. This lesson requires that the teacher understands complex theological and scientific truths, namely the Catholic doctrine of creation, Christ as the end (purpose/goal) of creation itself, the Theory of Evolution, and Cosmology. </span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong>Purpose:</strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>This lesson has multiple purposes:</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>1. to help students visualize and make sense of astronomical numbers such as millions of years  and understand the temporal relationship between major cosmological events, evolutionary events, and theological events.</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>2. to help students understand that creation is not one moment in time but the bringing into existence of time and the universe as a whole and that the universe is created both by and for Christ.</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>3. to help students understand that God reveals himself not only through his supernatural revelation in Jesus Christ but also in and through his natural revelation as well, which exists at every moment.</span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong>Timing:</strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>Total time needed: 120 minutes (two block periods or several smaller periods) plus one night of homework the day before the activity begins.</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>*There are five total timelines that will be created on the football field; a teacher may shorten the activity by removing one or more of the timelines. Do NOT remove the first or the final timeline, as this will remove the theological aspect of the activity.</span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong>Placement:</strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>When used in a Faith/Science senior elective, this activity can be used either before OR after the units concerning evolution and cosmology. When used before the evolution and cosmology units, this activity serves as an invitation to ask students to think critically about the Catholic Doctrine of creation before they fully understand it. When used after the evolution and cosmology units, this activity serves as the culmination of these two units and allows students to review/visualize what they have learned. The teacher decides what works best for his/her students.</span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong>Sources Needed BEFORE Class:</strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>-One copy of the activity packet for each student (provided in resources)</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>-Large poster boards or large printouts of EACH event on EACH timeline.*</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>*Printouts need to be large enough to be seen from a distance. (<strong><span>provided in resources</span></strong>)</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>-A 100-yard football field OR a hallway/sidewalk that is 100 yards (pre-measured)</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>-A camera (or cell phone camera) IF you have the ability to stand above the timeline (to take pictures of the timelines once they are completed).</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>-If you are doing this activity outdoors, a megaphone is recommended!</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong>Format:</strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>1. Homework the night before the activity:</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>-Provide students with copies of the activity packet (provided in resources) and ask students to answer the <strong><span>pre-activity questions</span></strong> AND the timeline scale calculations needed for each timeline.</span></span></span><br />  </p> <p><span><span><span>2. Main Portions of the Activity:</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>a. Lead a full-class discussion covering the <strong><span>pre-activity questions</span></strong> listed in the activity packet.</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>b. Provide students with a basic understanding of what they will be doing on the football field (sidewalk, etc.).  NOTE: Students will need pencils and calculators on the field (to complete the packet and to correct possible errors in calculations from the night before.)</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>c. Bring students (and your supplies) out to the location where this activity will be completed.</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>d. Create each timeline on the football field according to the instructions in the activity packet. To create the first timeline, give each student a random event/sign from the<br /> timeline and ask each student to determine (mathematically) where on the football field he/she should stand (keep in mind that some students may need easier events<br /> according to their abilities). *Pair up students or create small groups as needed, depending on how large your class is. Once students have placed themselves on the correct location on the field, ask students to hold up their signs so all other students can read the signs.  </span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong>IMPORTANT: DO NOT SKIP THIS STEP</strong>:</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>Go to the student standing at the Big Bang, and READ THIS SECTION from the Prologue of the Gospel of John: “In the beginning was the Word: the Word was with God and the word was God. He was with God in the beginning. Through him all things came into being, not one thing came into being except through him” (John 1:1-3).  Next, walk to the middle of the field, where there are NO students/events present on the field and read the following from the Prologue of the Gospel of John: “What has come into being in him was life, life that was the light of men; and light shines in the darkness, and darkness could not overpower it” (John 1: 4-5). Finally, walk to the student who represents the Incarnation of Christ and read the following: “The Word became flesh, he lived among us, and we saw his glory, the glory that he has from the Father as only Son of the Father, full of grace and truth” (John 1:14). Ask students to evaluate the completed timeline and the Scripture passages read with the timeline. Lead a discussion (on the field) as you see fit. It is important to guide students to the understanding that the <em>logos</em> has been present in every moment of creation and that creation is not one fixed moment in time.</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>***DON’T FORGET TO TAKE A PICTURE OF YOUR COMPLETED TIMELINE (if you are able to view the timeline from bleachers or somewhere similar).  Once this timeline is complete, have students return their signs to you and move on to the next timeline. Continue in this manner until all timelines have been completed, depending on how much time you decide to devote to this activity. *SOME TIMELINES CAN BE COMPLETED FOR HOMEWORK (teacher discretion).</span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span>e. Once you have completed all of the timelines that you wish to complete outside of the classroom, have the students return to the classroom. Assign the following  homework: students should complete the post-activity questions for homework and prepare for a full-class discussion the following day. NOTE: if time permits, students can complete the post-activity questions in class if the teacher wishes. </span></span></span><br /> <br /> <span><span><span>f. ***That evening (or while the students are working on their post-activity questions in class), do not forget to upload the pictures of the completed timelines that were taken<br /> when the students were on the football field into a powerpoint (or something similar). This will give students a good visual to help guide the full-class discussion!  Lead a full-class discussion over the post-activity questions in the activity packet. Be sure to cover the items listed in the  Essential Questions and Knowledge sections of this lesson plan!</span></span></span></p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN"><span><span>The assessment for this assignment is the completed Activity Packet (provided in resources).</span></span></span><strong><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN"><span><span> </span></span></span></strong></p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-standards--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-standards.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-standards.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-standards field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Standards</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong>Theological Standards (USCCB Framework):</strong><br />  A. field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">This 9th grade biology lesson will help students discern that scientific reason does not conflict with the ongoing development of creation. The first thing Sacred Scripture tells us about God is that He created: “In the beginning God created the heavens and the earth” Gen 1:1. This is an essential article of belief among Christians. Scripture reveals that the Christian Doctrine of Creation contains four elements that reveal creation is an ongoing process. Some of the processes of creation can be understood through scientific inquiry. <br /> </div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Reinforce knowledge of how God created the world </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>from nothing, with time, freely, </span></em><span>and</span><em><span> by the Trinity </span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>through the completion of an introduction reading.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Recall and apply the foundations of Natural Selection as a mechanism for Evolution.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Expand on Genesis Creation accounts to lead to an understanding that Creation is ongoing.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Previous night’s homework:  </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Read synopsis of Dr. Chris Baglow’s chapter 3 found in</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span> Faith, Science, and Reason Theology on the Cutting Edge</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> (pg. 58-63)  Fill in notes from the reading for the next day. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Resource: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><a href="https://drive.google.com/open?id=19QTFffkzcZrlDPbm-1shSahM1MLuB1Bv">Synopsis of "The Christian Doctrine of Creation" by Dr. Chris Baglow</a> (Editable version found in Files)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Warm-up (5 minutes):</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1. Quick review of previous night’s reading questions</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>2. Worksheet Resource: </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://drive.google.com/open?id=1nZL9u0w51yucVgrzqDAykTw6IdDWNeak"><span><span><span><strong><em><span><span>Creation and Evolution-Think, Pair, Share.docx</span></span></em></strong></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><strong><em><span>  </span></em></strong><span>(Editable version and teacher key found in Files)</span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Think pair share groups (1 question for each of the 3 groups)(10-12 minutes): </span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1. What is the relationship between order found in Creation and God’s act of Creation?</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>2. Do you think there is conflict or unity between the idea of creation and the theory of evolution</span></span></span></span></span></span>?</p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>3. Discuss the difference between theory and law. Are there laws that govern the universe without changing? </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Video (15 minutes):</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> (Editable worksheet found in Files)</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>"Creation and Evolution"-Catholic Central (6:50)</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=B_sE07heyy4"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=B_sE07heyy4</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Possible Video Questions:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1. What is the Catholic view of evolution? </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>2. In what way do science and the Bible align regarding creation? </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>3. Science is defined by its observation and measurement of the physical world, so why can science not say definitively that God has no hand in creation? </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>4. What do you think it means to say that “God hasn’t stopped shaping the universe”? </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Collaborative Discussion (10 minutes): </span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1. Revisit essential questions.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>  A. What is the relationship between order found in Creation and God’s act of Creation?</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>     a. Teacher-guiding questions: From the Baglow reading review the meaning of creation </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>from nothing, with time, freely and by the Trinity.</span></em></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>  B. In terms of the ideas of creation and evolution do you find conflict or unity?</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>     a. Teacher-guiding questions: Be sure to clarify the difference between an expected/perceived conflict and a true conflict of principles.    </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>  C. Are there laws that govern the universe without changing? Explain your answer. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>     a. Teacher-guiding questions: Ask students for specific laws and be sure they are not confusing theories and laws.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>     b. Teacher-guiding questions: Be sure to provide solid examples such as the Law of gravity, Law of conservation of Mass and Kepler’s Laws of Motion.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>2. Does the new information change your previous ideas on Creation and evolution and the assumed conflict between faith and science? </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>3. Revisit Dr. Baglow paper and questions. Review student answers and provide brief feedback.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Rethink/Post Assessment (10 minutes): *If time allows/homework</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1. As a group, creatively develop a higher level statement about the Synopsis of </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>The Christian Doctrine of Creation</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> by Dr. Chris Baglow reading as you understand it. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>2. Primary source reading (St. Augustine on the Literal Interpretation of Genesis, City of God, 11:6, 419 AD)</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>3. Class discussion of topic</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Extra Credit: </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Read the article, “Can Catholics believe in both God and evolution” by Fr. Jason Signalness and write a 100 word reflection paragraph about the article.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><a href="https://bismarckdiocese.com/news/can-catholics-believe-in-both-god-and-evolution"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>https://bismarckdiocese.com/news/can-catholics-believe-in-both-god-and-evolution</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Pre-assessment: </span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Warm-up questions</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Summative evaluation:</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Synopsis of The Christian Doctrine of Creation questions</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Final post-assessment student created question</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-standards--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-standards.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-standards.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-standards field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Standards</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span><span><span>USCCB II.V.Challenges </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>A. How can we know God really exists? </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>2. By looking around at creation, reason and experience can point to God’s existence (CCC, nos. 156-159).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The order and beauty of the natural world</span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>point to God as the origin and Creator of the</span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>universe (CCC, no. 295).</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Creation did not happen by chance;</span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>throughout history the Church has taught that someone had to be behind it, and that someone is God (CCC, nos. 156, 295).</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The natural law written upon each person’s heart and the longing for God that each person has also point to God’s existence (CCC, nos. 1954-1960).</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>USCCB I.VI. E. 1. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>E. Why do Catholics maintain beliefs and practices that are not in the Bible?</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The Bible is not the sole means that God chose to hand on the truths of revelation. Scripture and Tradition are the two complementary ways revelation is passed down (CCC, nos. 80, 97).</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>USCCB II.II. C. 1. a.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>C. The Three Divine Persons of the Trinity.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The First Person of the Trinity: God the Father (CCC, nos. 238-242).</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>God the Father is the source of all that is,</span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>visible and invisible.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>USCCB III. A-D</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>III. Understanding Scripture</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>A. Authentic interpretation of the Bible is the responsibility of the teaching office of the Church (CCC, nos. 85-87, 100).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><em><span>Divino Afflante Spiritu </span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>(Pius XII, 1943; permitted</span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>limited use of modern methods of biblical criticism).</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><em><span>Dei Verbum </span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>(DV) (Vatican II, 1965; Church teaching on revelation</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Pontifical Biblical Commission, </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Interpretation of the Bible in the Church</span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>, 1993,    nos. 5-19.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>B.  Criteria for interpreting the Sacred Scripture (CCC, nos. 109-114, 137).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1. read and interpret Sacred Scripture within the tradition and teaching of the Church.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>2. Give attention both to what the human authors intended to say and to what God reveals to us by their words.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>3. Take into account the conditions of the time when it was written and the culture where it was written.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>4. read and interpret Sacred Scripture in the light of the same Holy Spirit by whom it was written (DV, nos. 12-13).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>5. read and interpret each part of Sacred Scripture with an awareness and understanding of the unity of the content and teaching of the entire Bible.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>6. Be attentive to the analogy of faith, that is, the unity that exists in all Church teaching.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>C. Senses of Scripture (CCC, nos. 115, 118-119).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1. The literal sense: the meaning conveyed by the words of Scripture and discovered by exegesis (CCC, nos. 109-110, 116).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>D. The Bible in relation to science and history (CCC, nos. 37, 159, 1960)</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The Church teaches us how to relate truths of faith to science.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>There can be no conflict between religious truth and scientific and historical truth (CCC, no. 159).</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The difference between the Catholic understanding of Scripture and that of those who interpret the Bible in an overly literalist, fundamentalist way or with an approach limited to a symbolic understanding.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>NGSS </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>       HSESS 1-6  Scientific reasoning and evidence to account for Earth’s formation</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>HS-LS4-1.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Communicate scientific information that common ancestry and biological evolution are supported by multiple lines of empirical evidence. </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>[Clarification Statement: Emphasis is on a conceptual understanding of the role each line of evidence has relating to common ancestry and biological evolution. Examples of evidence could include similarities in DNA sequences, anatomical structures, and order of appearance of structures in embryological development.]</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>MS-PS1-5.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Develop and use a model to describe how the total number of atoms does not change in a chemical reaction and thus mass is conserved. </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>[Clarification Statement: Emphasis is on law of conservation of matter and on physical models or drawings, including digital forms, that represent atoms.]</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span> </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>[</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Assessment Boundary: Assessment does not include the use of atomic masses, balancing symbolic equations, or intermolecular forces.</span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>]</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>HS-PS2-4.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Use mathematical representations of Newton’s Law of Gravitation and Coulomb’s Law to describe and predict the gravitational and electrostatic forces between objects.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>PS2.B: Types of Interactions</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Newton’s law of universal gravitation and Coulomb’s law provide the mathematical models to describe and predict the effects of gravitational and electrostatic forces between distant objects.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Forces at a distance are explained by fields (gravitational, electric, and magnetic) permeating space that can transfer energy through space. Magnets or electric currents cause magnetic fields; electric charges or changing magnetic fields cause electric fields.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span> </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>[Clarification Statement: Emphasis is on both quantitative and conceptual descriptions of gravitational and electric fields.] [</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Assessment Boundary: Assessment is limited to systems with two objects.</span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>]</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from
